- [x] **Orphan-scan false-positive noise** — meeting notes often phrase action items differently from their TODO.md counterparts (e.g. full paths vs basename, bold markers shifting word positions), so the 4-word key match fails and already-done items are flagged as orphans every meeting. Root cause: key4 is extracted after `**` stripping but before backtick/path simplification. Options: (a) strip backtick content before key extraction; (b) extract only the first non-punctuation token as a label (e.g. `N9b-1.` or `Sc3.`) and match that against TODO.md; (c) only scan meeting notes newer than the last `[x]`-closure date. **Closed 2026-05-14** — superseded by `docs/meeting-notes/2026-05-14-1803-orphan-scan-accumulation.md`. Root fix: union-read `TODO.md + TODO.archive.md` (D1) + SKILL.md Step 5b process discipline (D2). Options (a)/(b)/(c)/anchor-marker all withdrawn.

- [x] **Workflow profiler for the /relay loop — real numbers, no observation bias** (done 2026-06-15: `relay/scripts/profile-run.sh <runId|wf-id|wf-dir>` + `tests/test_profile_run.sh`; emits concurrency-over-time vs cap, a blocked-vs-`queued-behind-cap` round-boundary verdict, and per-phase/per-model aggregates) — user 2026-06-15: recurring "I think I saw a single Haiku being waited for before another discovery round" suspicion that can't be settled by eyeballing `/workflows`. Emit: (a) a **concurrency-over-time** curve (how many agents live at each instant) against the harness cap `min(16, cores-2)`; (b) a **round-boundary analysis** — the gap between round N's last integration and round N+1's first `discover-prelude`, and exactly which agents (and models) occupy it; (c) per-label / per-phase aggregates (count, total/avg duration, total tokens). Tool: `relay/scripts/profile-run.sh <runId|wf-dir>`. **Settles the Haiku question with data**: post-cb50 there is no *logical* await of status writes between rounds (scheduleStatusWrite is fire-and-forget; `await statusTail` only at run END) — BUT a queued Haiku status-write can still occupy 1 of the ~6 cap slots and *delay the prelude's start under cap contention*, which LOOKS like "discovery waiting for a Haiku" without being a logic block. The profiler distinguishes "blocked-on" from "queued-behind-under-cap". Token usage falls out for free (cost-per-round, cost-per-verdict-class). <!-- id:a59e -->

- [x] **Cross-session lease LEAKS when a child dies without integrating (release is coupled to the integration path); + no heartbeat means long children can lose their lease mid-work** (done 2026-06-16, strong-execute) — fixes (a)+(b) landed: `runUnit` now calls `releaseLease(unit)` in a per-unit FINALLY path after the child settles with ANY outcome (merged/handback/null/error), run-scoped + idempotent vs. the integrator's retained step-0 release (defense-in-depth), and guarded against the review→execute re-chain steal window (`rechainedSameRepo`); claim.sh gained worktree-anchored liveness (a stale-mtime claim whose recorded `--worktree` still has commits beyond main is LIVE — the converse of id:3ac8 — so a >TTL long child isn't stolen mid-work) plus a `heartbeat` subcommand and a `worktree` shard field, and the work child now passes `--worktree` to acquire. (c) TTL shortening deferred — leave at 1800s now that liveness no longer depends solely on it. Tests: `tests/test_relay_claim_liveness.sh` (heartbeat + worktree-anchored staleness, hermetic git repos) and new id:7570 static checks in `tests/test_relay_loop_structure.sh`. Suite 59/0. — observed live 2026-06-16 (run relay-20260616-112222-29307, round 9): another session was blocked from writing mathematical-writing's TODO/ROADMAP because "a live relay run holds mathematical-writing (mode hard, since 13:18)" — but that hard child was DEAD: worktree `…/mathematical-writing/relay-…-29307-hard` had HEAD==main (0 commits) and zero file activity for 16 min, and there was no integrate/handback event for it. The lease (id:ebfb) stayed held by the ephemeral dead pid 1202111 until its 30-min TTL, needlessly deferring the other session. **Manually released** via `claim.sh release mathematical-writing --run relay-20260616-112222-29307`. (Likely cause of the child death itself: math-writing is Lean/Mathlib — memory-heavy — so an OOM-killed hard child is plausible; cf. [[oom-local-model-session-kills]] — but the LEAK is the bug here regardless of why the child died.) **Root cause (relay-loop.js):** (1) lease release lives INSIDE the integrate agent (L940 step 0); a child that returns null/errors/dies SKIPS integration (L1041/1045 catch → recoverable-handback path), so the release never runs → lease leaks for the full TTL. (2) The claim `pid` is the ephemeral shell that ran `claim.sh acquire`, NOT the agent — so it's useless as a liveness signal (always "dead" within seconds). (3) NO heartbeat: claim mtime is fixed at acquire time and TTL=1800s, so a LEGITIMATELY-long child (>30 min) would have its lease EXPIRE mid-work → another run grabs the repo → double-work/collision (the converse failure, worse than a leak). **Fixes:** (a) immediate — release the lease in a per-unit FINALLY path (after the child settles with ANY outcome: integrate, handback, null, error), not only inside integration; (b) tie claim liveness to the HELD WORKTREE (reuse the id:3ac8 worktree-staleness signal: a claim whose worktree HEAD==main with no recent mtime is stale) and/or HEARTBEAT the claim mtime while the child is alive, so both the leak AND the long-child-expiry directions become correct; (c) optionally shorten TTL once (a)+(b) land. Relates to id:ebfb (lease registry), id:0902 (interactive claim-aware), id:3ac8 (worktree-staleness reap — the analog liveness signal claims should share), id:0547 (same-repo race), id:719e (reliability/waste). <!-- id:7570 -->

- [x] **`--afk` pool reports an INTENSIVE-only repo as "idle — no open work" instead of dispatching the INTENSIVE unit** (observed 2026-06-23 `/relay --afk`, run relay-20260623-112409) — ai-codebench has an open `[INTENSIVE — local-llm]` item (id:244b, ~15 model runs pending) and the run set `allowIntensive=true`, yet the discovery shard classified the repo `idle — in sync, no open work` and never emitted an intensive-tagged unit, so `relay-loop.js`'s INTENSIVE partition (L877, `ALLOW_INTENSIVE ? intensiveUnits : intensiveDeferred`) never got a unit to dispatch. **Not a gather bug:** `gather-repo-state.sh --repo ai-codebench` correctly emits `is_finished=false`, the open `[INTENSIVE]` box, and id:244b (verified this session). **Root cause = shard JUDGMENT:** the shard never sees the `--afk`/`allowIntensive` flag (it's a JS-level decision), and the repo's own ROADMAP convention prose says *"a session finding only `[INTENSIVE]` items open reports 'no executor-eligible work' and stops"* — written for generic/remote executors with no GPU. The shard reads that prose literally and reports the repo idle, short-circuiting the intended design (always emit an intensive unit; let the loop decide dispatch by `ALLOW_INTENSIVE`). **Fix direction:** make the discover-shard prompt treat an open `[INTENSIVE — <res>]` item as WORK unconditionally — emit a unit with `intensive` set and NEVER report idle for it — leaving the auto-run-vs-defer decision to `relay-loop.js` (it already surfaces deferred intensive units as skipped when `!ALLOW_INTENSIVE`). The repo-local "reports no executor-eligible work" convention must not override the shard's emit. Add a shard-canary case: INTENSIVE-only open repo → classified as an intensive unit, not idle. Distinct from id:000d (false-dispatch on FINISHED repos — the inverse) and a natural check to fold into the relay-health report id:0907. Directly blocked the user's overnight ai-codebench drain (id:244b/8bea). **Promoted to ROADMAP [ROUTINE] (review Run 47, single-id-two-views) with acceptance + red spec `tests/test_relay_loop_intensive_emit.sh`.** <!-- id:ad74 -->
- [x] **Recurring `[HARD — pool]` audit (id:401c) spins forever when it's the only open item — vacuous self-audit loop burns Opus** — DONE 2026-06-23 (both mechanisms shipped, suite 91/0/0): gather `substantive_unaudited`+`work_sig` primitive (ignores the pool's own `relay: checkpoint` commits) + mechanism 1 shard recurring-audit gate (id:401c marked `relay:recurring-audit`, idled when nothing new to audit) + mechanism 2 deterministic `redispatchGuard` circuit breaker (suppress any non-injected (repo,verdict) dispatched >3× with unchanged work_sig; injected exempt). (observed 2026-06-23 `/relay --afk`, run relay-20260623-172446) — once every genuine `[ROUTINE]`/`[HARD — pool]` item in dotclaude-skills had drained, **id:401c (the RECURRING strong-model audit, which never closes by design) became the only open pool-dispatchable item**, so the `hard` verdict (id:da26) re-selected it EVERY round. Each round audited "commits since last checkpoint" — but the only commit since the prior round WAS that round's own `relay: checkpoint …` commit, so every audit reported *"LEDGER-ONLY clean by vacuity — no findings"* and wrote a fresh checkpoint, which the next round then audited. **~13 consecutive vacuous rounds (audit Run 55→67, ~20:01–21:47, ~9 min each) drove the 5h quota bucket 98%→41% for ZERO output**, and each checkpoint commit changed HEAD → invalidated the discover-sig cache (id:c3a6) → forced a re-classify, so the cache couldn't damp it. **Root cause:** a never-closing recurring HARD item + no guard for "the audit window contains only the pool's own checkpoint commits." **Fix directions:** (a) the `hard` scheduler (or the 401c audit step) must treat an audit window of ONLY relay-checkpoint commits (no real/new code-or-ledger commits) as **nothing-to-audit → idle/skip**, not a dispatch (mirrors the id:000d is_finished demote-guard, generalized to "no NEW auditable work"); (b) a per-item **cooldown / min-interval** on recurring HARD items (e.g. don't re-fire id:401c more than once per N hours or until ≥1 non-ckpt commit lands); (c) make a recurring audit's "open" state CONDITIONAL — it's only dispatchable when there are unaudited *substantive* commits since `last_review`/`last_strong_ckpt`, else it sits dormant. Without this, ANY repo that drains to "only the recurring audit open" will silently spin and burn the apex tier. Caught only because the user asked "stuck or catching up?"; a natural check to fold into the relay-health report (id:0907) AND a strong argument for the exit-reason/idle-detection work (id:8602). Relates id:401c (the recurring audit), id:da26 (`hard` verdict steady-state), id:000d (finished-repo demote guard — the analogue), id:c3a6 (sig cache, defeated by the ckpt-commit churn). <!-- id:365b -->
- [x] **DONE 2026-06-23 (shipped + tested) — First-class per-run priority + exclusion args for the autonomous pool — `--priority <repo[s]>` / `--exclude <repo[s]>` without mutating relay.toml** — `relay-loop.js` reads `args.priorityRepos`/`args.excludeRepos`: EXCLUDE drops repos from the own list before sharding (skipped `excluded for this run (--exclude)`, no relay.toml write); PRIORITY is a per-run within-class ordering bump (above income, below injected + D3 verdict class), reorders the repo's natural unit only (no double-dispatch — the finding). Unknown names LOUD-rejected/surfaced. Logic in pure helper `relay/scripts/pool-args.mjs` (byte-equiv inline copies pinned by `tests/test_relay_pool_args.sh`); SKILL.md front door documents both run-scoped flags. ROADMAP id:d530. — observed 2026-06-23 (`/relay --afk priority on zkm-stt, exclude codebench-ai`): the front door has NO arg for either, so both had to be hand-worked: priority via `inject.sh add zkm-stt` (the raw script — abuses the user-injection mechanism id:baf1, which is really "do this NEXT/once", not "this repo ranks higher all run"), and exclusion via a **temporary `classification = "own"->"excluded"` edit to relay.toml** that must be manually reverted after the run (a destructive mutation of the sticky registry — survives a session-kill mid-run = silent permanent exclusion). Neither is a clean per-invocation knob. **Goal:** `/relay [--afk] --priority <repo|repo,repo> --exclude <repo|repo,repo>` (also accept the natural-language forms the user typed) parsed by the front door and passed as `args.priorityRepos` / `args.excludeRepos` into `relay-loop.js`, scoped to THIS run only, registry untouched. Semantics to design: **priority** = bump those repos to the front of slot contention WITHIN their verdict class (a per-run tier above `income`, but still under the D3 verdict-class order + injected-unit precedence — NOT a verdict override), distinct from `inject` (which forces a one-shot unit); **exclude** = the discovery shards simply never emit a unit for those repos (surface them in `RELAY_STATUS.md` Skipped as "excluded for this run (--exclude)"), no relay.toml write. Reject unknown/unconfirmed repo names LOUDLY (id:415b grammar). **Observed 2026-06-23 (same session):** approximating priority via `inject.sh add zkm-stt` caused a REDUNDANT DOUBLE-DISPATCH — the injected unit ran ahead AND normal discovery still emitted its own zkm-stt execute unit the same round (events log: two `dispatch repo=zkm-stt mode=execute round=1`; the 2nd integrate logged "already pushed (integration completed by previous relay run); worktree already cleaned"). Concrete proof that priority must be an ORDERING bump within the verdict class, NOT a separate injected unit (which `inject` is) — `--priority` must dedupe against / merge with the repo's naturally-discovered unit, never add a second one for the same repo. Relates id:354f (`/relay inject` — the one-shot cousin), id:1ffc (richer income ranking — priority could read the same weight), id:a02c (uniform scope-arg grammar — `--exclude` is the inverse of a repo-list scope), id:11c6 (front-door arg parsing). Natural fold into the scope-arg-grammar work. <!-- id:d530 -->

CONFIRMED repro (isochrone): `orphan-scan.sh --cross-ledger` reports `id:f4a7 — TODO:[x] ROADMAP:[ ]`, but the actual `<!-- id:f4a7 -->` token line is `- [ ]` in BOTH files and NO `[x]` line anywhere contains the string `f4a7` (the id is also mentioned in prose on 3 sibling child lines `f4a7-A/B/C`, all `[ ]`). Control: `id:601e` in the same repo is reported correctly (genuinely `[ ]` TODO / `[x]` ROADMAP). So the check mis-attributes a checkbox NOT belonging to the id's own token line — likely a substring / multi-mention / adjacent-id confusion in how it pairs the id to a checkbox (it must correlate STRICTLY on the single line bearing `<!-- id:XXXX -->`, exact-token, not a prose/substring match). **Why it matters:** this is the interim TODO↔ROADMAP drift backstop that id:2840 leans on AND a relay-doctor input (id:9bec) — a noisy mix of real + phantom drift erodes trust in both. **Acceptance:** a hermetic test with (a) an id whose token lines agree but whose id is mentioned in prose on other lines → reported CLEAN; (b) a genuine token-line disagreement → reported DRIFT; orphan-scan correlates only the `<!-- id:XXXX -->`-bearing line's checkbox. [ROUTINE] — done 2026-06-24 (fix shipped d2a9d98 + hermetic test; TODO twin ticked by review) <!-- id:9221 -->

- [x] **Add an output-style rule to global `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`: no clickbait/teaser prose in working sessions** — owner `/feedback` 2026-06-18: a code session must not emit content-free suspense sentences like *"Both engines agree on the splittable/badge mechanics — but with a critical asymmetry."* — a teaser that asserts something notable exists (a "critical asymmetry") WITHOUT naming it or its evidence on the same line. Diagnosed as Opus over-trained on clickbait register. **Proposed rule** (owner to ratify exact wording — CLAUDE.md is curated): under a reporting/communication heading, "State the finding, never tease it. Don't write a standalone sentence claiming significance ('a critical X', 'the surprising part') without immediately, in the same breath, giving the concrete thing and why. Lead with the fact; every significance-claim carries its evidence inline. No hype sentences before a table/finding." - [x] **`ckpt-tag.sh` hard-fails (exit 1) when a repo can't track `.gitattributes`** — observed 2026-06-30 reviewing `kienzler-homepage`, whose `.gitignore` had a `.*` dotfile catch-all that swallowed `.gitattributes`, so ckpt-tag's `git add -- RELAY_LOG.md .gitattributes` aborted the WHOLE checkpoint (no commit, no tag) and left `RELAY_LOG.md` staged. The `RELAY_LOG.md merge=union` attribute is a nicety (matters only for parallel relay merges), not essential — a repo that can't add it should still get its checkpoint. **Fix:** ckpt-tag.sh should degrade gracefully — try to stage `.gitattributes`, but on failure WARN + proceed with `RELAY_LOG.md` + tag only (don't abort). Workaround used 2026-06-30: manual `git commit RELAY_LOG.md` + `git tag -a`, and fixed kienzler's `.gitignore` (negated `!.gitattributes`/`!.dns/`). <!-- id:a7a3 -->

- [x] **Investigate the 2026-07-01 flip discovery-precision regressions + model the relay as a STATE MACHINE ("what touches what when" / invalid-state detection)** [HARD — meeting] (user 2026-07-01, from the a0b6-flip `/relay --once` smoke). **Two precision bugs the smoke surfaced** — both are the mechanical classifier (now authoritative post-flip) being LESS precise than the old LLM shard on real ledger shapes; caught by the executor's own size-out → clean handbacks (no damage), but wasteful (executor sessions spawned for nothing): **(1) `classify-verdict.sh` gates `execute` on `has_routine`** (ANY `[ROUTINE]` substring) instead of an actionable-routine signal (open, tag-anchored `[ROUTINE]`, `@manual`/human-gated EXCLUDED). `classify-repo.sh` computes `roadmap_actionable_open` but it MIXES routine+pool and isn't used for the execute gate → `yinyang-puzzle` (all `[ROUTINE]` @manual) mis-fired `execute`→handback. Need a distinct `actionable_routine_open` and gate `execute` on it — restores the id:e107 executor-actionable precision the flip dropped. **(2) `[ROUTINE]` detected by substring `"[ROUTINE]" in ln`, not tag-anchored** to the item's own bracket → `leAIrn2learn` matched `[ROUTINE]` inside id:c3f5's INLINE-HISTORY prose (a `[HARD — pool]` item) → phantom `execute` (same class as the id:1bbd HARD-lane prose-match fix; apply the backtick/prose-strip anchoring to the ROUTINE/execute path). **Fix both as executor-actionable RED-spec items** (fixtures: @manual-only repo → NOT execute; prose-`[ROUTINE]` → NOT execute). **BROADER (the reason to link — user-directed):** build a STATE-MACHINE / state-diagram model of the relay to fully grasp **what touches what when** — the artifact × actor × transition matrix (ROADMAP / TODO / REVIEW_ME / relay.toml / worktrees / leases / decision-queue / **main-checkout**, written/read by prelude / discover-run / executor / reviewer / integrator / id:3801 gate-detection / `/meeting`) — and **define validity invariants so 'invalid states' become detectable**. Two invalid states already observed: (i) an **uncommitted main-checkout edit** (loderite id:3801 gate-detection residue stranded dirty — the deeper fix is to make id:3801's main write COMMIT ATOMICALLY, id:148b flock+commit pattern, so it can't strand); (ii) an **`execute` verdict on a repo with no executor-actionable work** (the two bugs above). A formal state model turns both classes into a deterministic invalid-state DETECTOR (a relay-doctor id:9bec extension) instead of ad-hoc per-round discovery. Relate: id:4d8e (the flip umbrella), a0b6 (shipped), id:3801, id:e107, id:1bbd, id:148b, relay-doctor id:9bec. **PART-1 SHIPPED 2026-07-01 (relay-ckpt-20260701-2110):** the precision fixes landed — `classify-repo.sh` derives `actionable_routine_open` (open [ROUTINE], **primary-lane** = first lane-tag beats a fragile backtick-strip on 3.5k-char history lines, NOT @manual/human-gated, NOT dep-blocked "🚧/BLOCKED on"); `classify-verdict.sh` gates `execute` on it (−1 back-compat fallback). - [x] **Integrator mislabels a ZERO-COMMIT review branch as "duplicate dispatch" → handback, NO checkpoint → the audit window never closes and the pool re-dispatches strong reviews forever** [HARD — pool] — **done 2026-07-01** (same-night Fable bugfix child, merged + ckpt): relay-loop.js integrate distinguishes clean-empty-review (⇒ `ckpt-tag.sh -c <reviewed-tip>`, new flag) from genuine duplicate; destructive cleanup scoped to own-runId artifacts (id:6e02 hazard); worked_ids string-coercion fixed (`ids:["[","]"]` telemetry bug). Tests test_ckpt_tag_commit_target.sh + test_gather_stale_strong_watermark.sh; suite 158/0/0. (found by the 2026-07-01 fable catch-up review, from the run `relay-20260701-202806-14640` 20:36 handback). **Mechanism (verified against git timestamps + relay-events.jsonl):** the review child branched at the TRUE then-HEAD `33169ee` (20:20:36; next main commit `65ce4ea` landed 20:34:53 — the child did NOT see a stale main), made **zero commits** (a clean review window with no ledger delta is legitimate: commit-ledger.sh no-ops), so its branch tip stayed == its base == an ancestor of the (meanwhile advanced) main. The integrator's `git merge --no-ff` said "Already up to date" and it concluded "**Duplicate dispatch** — no integration action performed": no ckpt tag, no relay.toml update, handback. Consequences: (a) the misleading label masks the real state ("clean review, nothing to integrate"); (b) the reviewed window is never checkpointed, so the NEXT discovery re-classifies the same commits as unaudited and re-spends a strong review child — an unattended pool can loop this indefinitely; (c) tonight it also compounded the relay.toml staleness (id:0a3b). **Fix (the design nuance that makes this pool-lane, not ROUTINE):** the integrator must distinguish `tip == base ∧ zero commits` (clean empty review → **checkpoint at the reviewed tip**, i.e. tag the child's base/tip commit — NOT current main HEAD, which may contain newer commits the review never saw and must not be marked audited) from a genuine duplicate (branch already merged by an earlier integrator in the SAME run). Surface in relay-loop.js integrate() prompt (:1424 area) + a fixture test (zero-commit branch + advanced main → ckpt at branch tip, no handback). Relates: invariant I8/id:333c (ckpt bookkeeping), id:9d2b backtest (re-review waste), the 2026-07-01 events-log evidence. <!-- id:8e3e -->

Commit or move the changes, then run 'git push' manually."* **Root cause:** `~/.claude` is a worktree of the claude-diary repo whose tree is **perpetually dirty with harness RUNTIME churn** — tracked `.last-cleanup` + `history.jsonl` (rewritten constantly) and untracked `plans/`, `session-env/`, `sessions/`, `tasks/` (NOT gitignored). Prefer (b)+(c): the guard should reason about the actual commit, not the whole tree, and never assert an unverified cause. - [x] **[HARD — pool] Discovery-queue verdict/state coherence — content-address the CASE A copy (per-repo `discover-sig` stamped in the queue; copy only on queue-sig == live-sig) + sig-echo as mangle canary** (Fable review 2026-07-08) — three verified gaps in the id:7402 consumption path: (1) `relay-loop.js:914-923` trusts `latest.json` MTIME alone — a repo whose live sig just flagged CHANGED still gets the ≤20-min-old snapshot verdict copied (executor commits at T; snapshot from T−10min says execute/idle → the required `review` never fires), and `:969` then caches that stale verdict under the NEW live sig so it outlives the freshness window; (2) a repo that goes dirty AFTER the snapshot bypasses the classify `blocked` guard (live reconcile surfaces nothing → stale non-blocked verdict copied) — bounded only by the executor-side clean-tree gate; (3) the Haiku bridge-copy is shape-validated (SHARD_SCHEMA) but never content-checked against the queue bytes it just cat'd — a mangled copy that drops `is_finished`/`open_hard_pool`/`top_intensive`/`work_sig` silently DISARMS the id:000d/9973/ad74/365b backstops (missing fields default 0/''/false = never fire). - [x] **[MEETING] Sandboxing: run Claude / `/relay` as a separate OS user** — so auto-mode can't break anything beyond that user's permissions (group setup on `~/src`, write-isolation, polkit interaction). Motivated by the probe's invocation design (see `docs/meeting-notes/2026-06-17-0905-model-probe-tos-and-band.md` D1); broader scope warrants its own design meeting. **Child use-case 2026-07-07 (id:ec23):** run the UNATTENDED mechanical discovery producer (id:9d97 `.timer`) as a write-restricted OS user — write only its output dirs (`~/.config/relay/discovery-queue/`, heartbeat, logs), NO write to repos or `~/.cache/relay/worktrees` → a future code regression that reaches a destructive git op becomes an OS-denied LOUD failure, not a silent `rm`. Defense-in-depth outer layer above the fail-closed reconcile fix (id:e0f8); folds into this meeting's scope. **Two more use-cases 2026-07-08 (Fable review):** (i) the mechanical-run daemon (id:b3d0) `bash -c`'s relay-authored recipe cmds unattended, and its drop-dir trust boundary ("only a relay reviewer session writes pending/") is documented, NOT enforced — `~/.config/relay/recipes/pending` is plain user-writable and the `.path` unit auto-fires on any write; running daemon + producer under the same write-restricted OS user turns a forged/compromised recipe into an OS-denied loud failure (see id:1cb8 for the daemon's mechanical hardening). (ii) The id:af30 launch-wall: a dedicated sandboxed OS user (the model-probe id:2d01 ToS-reviewed precedent — subscription `claude -p` as its own user with empty `~/.claude`) is the structural answer to "headless pool relaunch needs `--dangerously-skip-permissions`" — inside a write-scoped user that flag stops being a blanket bypass; resolving it also unblocks eliminating the D3 residual queue-read (id:7402, per-round relaunch becomes possible). This meeting should therefore rank the sandbox as the LEAD permission strategy, with the broker-instance path (b444 transport / long-lived interactive session) as the human-INPUT channel, not the permission solution. Keep the [[anthropic-agent-sdk-billing-deferred]] hedge: headless `claude -p` volume economics may flip on the billing cutover — advance notice promised. **AGENDA ADD 2026-07-08 (user found `permissionMode: auto` default in `/config`):** constraint-archaeology question — does the af30 launch-wall still bind under a default-auto permissionMode? CAUTION (Fable): auto mode is NOT skip-permissions dissolving the wall — the af30 governor was denied BY the auto-mode classifier, so auto mode is the thing that said no to the *persistent permission-bypassing loop*; but it plausibly changes the `claude -p` calculus for ordinary relay operations (headless under auto may auto-approve the allowlisted/read surface without `--dangerously-skip-permissions` at all, classifier as guard). Meeting should TEST empirically what a headless `claude -p "/relay --afk"` under permissionMode=auto actually gets approved/denied, per operation class, before designing the sandbox around the skip-permissions assumption — the cheapest outcome is that the sandbox only needs to cover the classifier's deny-tail, not a blanket bypass. **HELD 2026-07-08** — see `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-08-1214-sandboxing-relay-os-users.md`; decisions D1 (two users now: `relay-ro`/`relay-svc`, `relay-pool` scoped-deferred), D2 (per-dir ACLs on `~/.config/relay`; `~/src` reads free via DAC), D3 (hybrid `--user`+root-owned-units-in-`/etc/systemd/user`+hardening-directives for A/B, `--system` for C; file-based creds, polkit default-deny), D4 (measure-first: auto-mode deny-tail probe GATES skip-perms; sandbox=containment≠authorization), D5 (ssh-push boundary is preferred C repo-write). - [x] **[HARD — meeting] Formally PROVE component contracts (read-only / pure / idempotent) with Lean4, not only test them** — ✅ DECIDED 2026-07-08 (see docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-08-1337-lean4-relay-mechanization-substrate.md): Lean pilot, substrate REVISITABLE at island-2; follow-ups id:50c4 (relay-core repo) / id:82c4 (classify-verdict pilot) / id:ba31 (reconcile island 2, gated) / id:7746 (executor-lane doc) + routed:b8e5 (aae4 triad toolchain pin). — user 2026-07-07: tests sample; a proof covers all inputs. Explore machine-checked contracts for the safety-critical relay primitives (reconcile reap, the producer's read-only promise, claim/lease invariants) via Lean4. Big design meeting (scope, what's provable vs testable, the spec↔code gap, effort). Ties to the user's Lean interest and the ChidiAI **Grand Truth Triad** (.mw / toesnail / ChidiAI) — see routed relation to chidiai. Relates [[feedback-enforce-not-document-contracts]], [[inflownistration-term]], id:e0f8/758e (the test-based layers this would formalize). **Fable pre-meeting take 2026-07-08 (user asked how this relates to the sandbox d0c0/ec23):** COMPLEMENTS, does not replace — they guard DIFFERENT layers. The OS sandbox enforces the write BOUNDARY over all inputs immediately (it would have stopped the e0f8 near-miss: the read-only producer had no business writing worktrees at all), but it CANNOT stop an authorized-but-wrong action — the dispatch-side reconcile legitimately reaps worktrees, so a wrong-TARGET reap is invisible to any boundary enforcement; that logic layer is exactly where proofs add unique value. The crux is the spec↔code gap (bash is not directly provable); the pragmatic pilot shape: formalize the reap/claim/lease STATE MACHINE already half-specified in the id:4da4 matrix + invariants I1–I9 (`docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-01-2142-relay-state-machine-invalid-state-detector.md`), prove ~2 invariants in Lean4 ("reap-set ∩ live-claims = ∅ in every reachable state"; "absent/unknown claim context ⇒ reap-set = ∅" — the e0f8 fail-closed rule), then GENERATE conformance test vectors from the model and run them against the bash (verified-reference-model pattern: the proof is exhaustive on the model, the vectors carry it to the code; the residual model↔code gap is pinned by the vectors and stated honestly, never claimed as proved). NB the mechanization work already built the precondition: classify-verdict.sh / the reconcile decision islands are pure JSON-in/JSON-out functions — the exact shape a Lean model can mirror 1:1. Sequencing: sandbox meeting first (days of effort, broad coverage, catches the observed incident class); this pilot second; neither gates the other. The meeting should resist scope creep beyond the one state machine — "prove the relay" is not the pilot. **RESCOPED 2026-07-08 (user): NOT Lean4-proofing bash — write the mechanization ITSELF in Lean4, bash only where unavoidable.** This supersedes the verified-reference-model/conformance-vector pattern above: the model↔code gap dissolves because the proven function IS the shipped code (Lean 4 compiles to native; `IO.Process` runs git; systemd runs the binary). Assessment (Fable): ~80% of the win is types-not-theorems — total JSON parsers (unknown/missing field = LOUD error, kills the backstop-disarm class id:4860-3), exhaustive verdict matches (kills the 0d58 substring class), one shared vocabulary type (kills the intensity/probe mismatch id:1cb8-6), no swallowed subshell exits (kills id:0fa0-a) — all by construction, zero theorems; the last 20% is proofs where they matter (reap invariants, fail-closed lemmas, 5ac6 "INTENSIVE never operative on human lanes" as a theorem). RELAY SYNERGY: a required named theorem is an UNGAMEABLE acceptance test — `lake build` + mandatory theorems cannot be faked green, strengthening the anti-gaming apparatus for delegated work. Architecture: plan/apply split — pure proven PLANNER (state → actions) + dumb effectful interpreter; the unproven rind (flock, tmp+mv, git exec) stays thin and typed. Strangler migration behind the EXISTING JSON contracts, reusing the a0b6 flip machinery (shadow → backtest parity → gated flip, bash fallback until N clean runs) — do NOT big-bang the week-old mechanical layer; land id:4860/0fa0/1cb8 in bash first. Pilot = port `classify-verdict` (pure JSON→JSON, fixture corpus + backtest replay = ready parity gate); island 2 = reconcile PLANNER w/ reap-invariant theorems (kills the havoc-reaper class at the root). MEETING must decide: toolchain/install story (public zero-dep repo + elan/lake — in-repo lake pkg vs sibling repo shipping a binary; the biggest real cost), island order + flip gates, executor-lane economics (Lean-w/-proofs = HARD-lane initially; theorem-gated delegation may flip that), what gets theorems vs types-only (`sorry`-free but theorem-light is a valid first rung), Lean-vs-Rust diligence question stated honestly (types-only would favor Rust's ecosystem; theorems + user's Lean investment justify Lean). **chidiAI / Grand-Truth correlation (user asked 2026-07-08):** the Lean relay core is the strongest rung of the triad's certainty-gating mesh (measure certainty → gate the action → degrade gracefully): (1) relay anti-gaming IS chidiAI's anti-bluff invariant in another substrate — an executor's "done, tests green" is a high-confidence/weak-verification claim (the exact case-law: `chidiai/docs/cases/2026-06-30-done-claim-tests-green-untested-clause.md`, our id:369c); a required named theorem is verification that CANNOT be bluffed, so theorem-backed modules can be gate-ASSERTed with cheaper review — i.e. tier the relay's own review depth by verification class, the mesh applied to the relay's review economics; (2) chidiAI's `VerificationBackend` protocol (chidiai id:79ee) already lists formal/Lean4 via the SHARED tier owned by mathematical-writing id:aae4 as a future concrete backend — the relay core is its first concrete target (routed:e470 to chidiai, gated on this pilot); the 23ab meeting must COORDINATE the toolchain/install choices with aae4 so elan/lake/binary decisions are made ONCE for the triad, not per-repo; (3) case-law symmetry: chidiAI's `docs/cases/` bluff library and the relay's RED-fixture corpus are the same epistemic pattern (each observed failure becomes machine-checked); a by-construction Lean fix retires whole case FAMILIES — record such retirements on both sides. **Distribution (user 2026-07-08):** GH releases work mechanically but clash with this repo's stated no-build/no-release/live-install-IS-published ethos → favor a SIBLING repo (`relay-core`) shipping per-arch binaries via its own GH releases with proper vX.Y.Z bump-and-tag (the versioning this repo deliberately lacks); the user-required opt-in ("`/relay` must work without it") falls out of the strangler FOR FREE — capability-detect the binary (PATH / `~/.local/bin`), else the bash path, the exact CASE A/CASE B fallback shape the discovery queue (id:7402) just shipped. Guard the house anti-pattern (derived-artifact drift): opt-in dual-path must NOT become permanent dual maintenance — once the flip gate passes, the bash twin FREEZES (bugfix-only), new behavior is Lean-only, and relay-doctor loudly reports "mechanical core absent — legacy bash path" so the fallback never silently ossifies. Full /relay repo split = separate trigger-gated question, id:a72c. <!-- id:23ab -->

- [x] **Reap a relay run's heartbeat on OBSERVED failure, not just TTL expiry — kill the redundant late watchdog popup** [ROUTINE] (observed 2026-07-07) — the outage watchdog (id:98f0) correctly notified that the `-c`-crash run (relay-...-174626) died, but ~1h LATE and REDUNDANTLY: the session had already detected the Workflow failure immediately (task-notification), relaunched, and reconciled the orphans within minutes — yet the dead heartbeat marker lingered because at relaunch it was only ~25min stale (under the ~3600s TTL), so auto-reconcile-on-restart (id:7809) didn't reap it; it aged past the TTL ~1h later and tripped the watchdog for a crash already resolved. - [x] **[HARD — meeting] Move the relay DISCOVERY loop off the Workflow engine so it can run mechanically (cron/systemd, free to curl/exec) — architecture call** (user 2026-07-01, from the id:2ec4 "can the Workflow JS just curl a local RPC?" question). The Workflow sandbox has **no network/shell/fs/subprocess** (confirmed `relay-loop.js:1529/1551` — `process.env` crashed the pool; a Haiku agent runs ONLY because "the sandbox has no shell/fs"), so `agent()` (a billed LLM) is the ONLY way to shell out from inside the loop. That is the *sole* reason discovery still spends an LLM round-trip after the a0b6 flip made it pure-transport (id:2ec4). **Alternative architecture:** run discovery as an ordinary cron/systemd script OUTSIDE the Workflow — free to `curl` a local RPC / `exec` `discover-repo.sh` directly, zero LLM — and only use a Workflow for the executor **dispatch** (which genuinely needs the managed `agent()` pool, [[relay-autonomous-pool-design]]). **The catch to resolve in the meeting:** the Workflow can't read a file/queue either (no fs), so handing per-round discovery results *into* the executor Workflow still needs one `agent()` read per round (via the existing prelude/inject path) UNLESS the whole loop leaves the Workflow engine — which means reimplementing executor parallelism (worktrees, leases, integrator, quota-stop) outside the pool. So it trades the discovery LLM shim for either (a) one residual `agent()` bridge-read per round (hybrid: cron discovery → queue → Workflow executor), or (b) abandoning the Workflow engine wholesale (lose the pool; own the parallelism). Design Qs: is the hybrid's single bridge-read cheaper than today's haiku prelude+run? does leaving the Workflow engine forfeit too much (the pool is WHY it's a Workflow)? does a cron discovery reintroduce the outage-resilience problem the Workflow-managed loop solved ([[relay-outage-resilience-design]], [[babysitter-durable-cron-no-op]])? Relate: id:2ec4 (the mechanical-tier forward-flag this splits from), [[relay-autonomous-pool-design]], id:98f0/7809 (watchdog/reconcile that already assume a local loop), id:a17a (state-diagram — the loop's engine boundary is exactly what a state model must draw). Gate: only worth it if the residual haiku discovery cost (measure per id:2ec4) proves material. **DECIDED 2026-07-07** (`docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-07-1228-relay-discovery-off-workflow.md`): reframed — the gate is NOT token cost but **reliability** (Haiku mangles even "exec+echo JSON"; rule = "no LLM if mechanical can do as good or better"). SPLIT: build the mechanical discovery producer now (id:9d97); residual queue-read stays deferred+labeled gated on the launch-wall (id:7402); two-liveness-domain heartbeat (id:54fc); wholesale-off-Workflow = trigger-gated contingency (id:882a). This umbrella stays open until the children land. <!-- children:9d97,7402,54fc --> <!-- id:65f9 -->
- [x] **[ROUTINE] `append.sh inbox-done XXXX` deletes EVERY checkbox line containing `routed:XXXX` — a cross-reference in another item's prose is collateral** (found 2026-07-10 while routing two chidiAI cases). `meeting/append.sh`'s inbox-done predicate is `needle in l and l.lstrip().startswith("- [")` with `needle = f"routed:{token}"` — a substring test, not an anchor. So an inbox item whose *prose* legitimately cites a sibling's token (e.g. "the contrast with `routed:4fa9` is the signal") is a checkbox line containing that needle, and resolving the sibling **silently deletes the citing item too**. inbox-done is destructive by design (vanish-on-resolve), and the inbox is local-only and never committed, so a wrongly-deleted item is **unrecoverable** — no git twin to restore from. Hit live this session: a praise-case item citing the offender case's token would have been destroyed by `inbox-done 4fa9`; worked around by writing the sibling token bare (`4fa9`, no `routed:` prefix), which is fragile convention, not a guard. **Fix:** anchor on the trailing marker comment `<!-- routed:XXXX -->` (the anchoring already mandated for the twin check in the global CLAUDE.md, and for typed edges id:46f6), not a bare substring; and refuse loudly (non-zero, write nothing) when the token matches ≠1 line. Same fail-open-substring class as id:1b1a (`md-merge.py update-ids` appends on an unmatched id) and id:0d58 (`[MECHANICAL]` substring false-positive) — a third instance, which argues the anchoring rule belongs in ONE shared helper rather than being re-derived per reader. Contract a test would verify: an item whose prose cites another's `routed:` token survives that other's `inbox-done`; a token matching two marker comments exits non-zero and deletes nothing. <!-- id:411d -->

- [x] [ROUTINE] **[HIGH PRIORITY] `md-merge.py update-ids` silently APPENDS an unmatched id — a typo'd token creates a duplicate ledger line instead of failing** (found 2026-07-10 while designing the typed-edge marker). `md-merge.py:143-152`: ids not present in the file are appended (anchored before the first archive heading, id:14d0). That is correct for *new* items but fail-OPEN for *updates*: a caller intending to edit `id:abcd` who mistypes it gets a silent second line, not an error — and the whole point of routing writes through this helper is that it is the SAFE path. Concretely, the near-miss this session: an inline `id:XXXX children:...` marker would not have matched `md-merge.py:135`'s `<!--\s*id:([0-9a-f]{4})\s*-->` regex, so every one of 18 intended in-place updates would have been appended as a duplicate. **Fix:** make intent explicit — updates fail LOUDLY on a miss (non-zero + named tokens on stderr); appends require an opt-in flag (`--allow-new` or a separate `add-items` subcommand). Then audit the ~10 readers that assume the id comment terminates immediately after the 4 hex digits (`orphan-scan.sh` ×6, `md-merge.py:135`, `handback-followup.py` ×3, `unpromoted-scan.sh` ×2, `backtest-historical.py`, `relay-doctor.sh`, `classify.sh:36`, `tests/run-tests.sh:33`). **Already broken today:** `handback-followup.py:71`'s `$`-anchored regex does not match `id:78ff`, whose id comment is followed by an `xledger-ok:` annotation — a pre-existing silent no-op, not introduced by the marker work. Contract a test would verify: `update-ids` with an unknown id exits non-zero and writes nothing; with `--allow-new` it appends as today; `handback-followup` appends its note to a line whose id comment is non-terminal. Relates id:46f6 (the typed-edge marker whose syntax this constrained), id:ee62 (visible-vs-comment annotations). `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-10-1430-typed-ledger-edges-umbrella-closure.md` <!-- id:1b1a -->
- [x] [ROUTINE] ** `orphan-scan.sh --shipped` never sees INDENTED sub-items — 14 of 241 open id-bearing TODO items (6%) are structurally invisible to every `--shipped` class** (found 2026-07-10 by the id:46f6 executor, confirmed against the live ledger). The shipped-mode driver greps `^- \[ \] ` anchored at column 0, so any `  - [ ] … <!-- id:XXXX -->` nested under a parent is never classified — not for TICK-READY, not for GATE-STALE, and now not for the typed-edge umbrella/gate classes either. - [x] [HARD — pool] ** Rehaul the cross-project inbox: an UNVERSIONED store with a DESTRUCTIVE resolve has no recovery path** (user 2026-07-10, after id:411d surfaced a live near-miss) — `~/.claude/todo-inbox.md` is **gitignored and untracked** (`~/.claude/.gitignore:42`), deliberately local-only because it names private repos. `append.sh inbox-done` is **vanish-on-resolve** (deletes the line, decided 2026-06-30) and matches on a **bare substring** (id:411d). Compose those three and a single mistyped or over-matching token **permanently destroys a pending routing item with no git twin, no archive, and no audit trail** — nothing to diff, nothing to restore. The stated safety premise ("the durable record is the committed `routed:XXXX` breadcrumb in the *target* repo") holds only when the delete is CORRECT; a WRONG delete removes the one copy of an item that was never written anywhere else. Today: 8 open items, and **3 non-conforming prose lines that `inbox-done` can never resolve** and no scanner can route — they will sit there forever. **CORRECTION 2026-07-10, same day, observed live:** direction (a) is **ALREADY SHIPPED for the AUTOMATIC path**. `relay/scripts/scan-routed.sh --apply` (id:678e slice 2) writes the `- [ ] [INBOUND routed:XXXX from <repo>]` stub into the target TODO via flock'd `md-merge.py`, commits it with `commit-ledger.sh`, and only THEN marks `inbox-done` — write-before-delete, idempotent. Witnessed this session: a parallel run drained all 9 open items into their targets (this repo ×2, chidiai ×3, loderite ×3, toesnail ×1) while I worked; my three chidiAI cases landed as INBOUND stubs and the inbox went to zero. I briefly read that as data loss — it was the mechanism working. **So the REAL residual is narrower than first written:** the risk lives on the **MANUAL `inbox-done XXXX`** path, which deletes with (i) no check that a twin exists in the target, and (ii) a bare-substring match (id:411d). That is the path a human/LLM invokes by hand — I used it twice this session. **Directions to weigh (decide the ordering):** (a) **make manual `inbox-done` refuse unless the target twin exists** (the auto path already proves the twin first) — or delete the manual verb entirely and route every resolve through `scan-routed.sh --apply`, which would dissolve this item. Evaluate FIRST. (b) back the inbox with an existing PRIVATE git repo — `~/.claude/projects` is itself a git repo with hourly `sessions(<host>)` auto-commits and is gitignored from `~/.claude`, so relocating the file there buys free history + recovery while staying unpublished (the same trick that made the memory-index before-state free, id:2e6d). (c) non-destructive resolve — move the line to a local `todo-inbox.archive.md` instead of deleting. (d) anchored, unique matching (**id:411d**, do this regardless — it is the cheap interim guard). (e) a conformance rule forbidding one item's prose from citing another's `routed:` token — weakest, guards a symptom. **Constraints:** must never be committed to a PUBLIC repo ([[feedback-no-leak-specifics-in-public-files]]); public-repo scripts must keep taking the path by injection, never hardcode it; keep the flock. Cousins: id:3947 (routed dead letters — same layer), id:678e (auto-reconcile, report-only), id:1b1a + id:0d58 (the same fail-open-substring class, which argues for ONE shared anchoring helper). Prefer *dissolving structurally over guarding* — see the design heuristics. — **DECIDED 2026-07-11 (meeting 1239, D4):** (b) relocate the inbox store into git-tracked `~/.claude/projects` FIRST (free history/recovery, stays private — dissolves "unversioned/no-recovery"), THEN (a-guard) make manual `inbox-done` refuse unless the target twin exists. - [x] **ROADMAP archiver orphans column-0 prose/blockquote bodies + leaves then-empty headers behind** (another project session, reported 2026-07-14). **DONE 2026-07-15** (relay handoff→exec→review, ROADMAP twin [x]): both `roadmap-archive.sh` + `archive-closed.sh` now capture column-0 prose/blockquote (boundary-model) and MOVE emptied transient headers into the archive adjacent to their items (user-decided; H1 + {Items,Current,Done,Backlog} protected); tests green + apex-reviewed + real-world reproduction confirmed. Two defects, both reproduced 2026-07-14 with a fixture (`scratchpad/rmtest`): **(1) prose/blockquote orphaning — `relay/scripts/roadmap-archive.sh` only.** Its `is_continuation()` treats a body line as part of the `[x]` item block *only if the line is blank or indented*; a **column-0 prose paragraph or `>` blockquote line** (common in ROADMAP item bodies — Session-note / Done-check / Context prose is frequently un-indented) is NOT recognised, so when the `- [x]` header moves to `ROADMAP.archive.md` its own body text is **left stranded in `ROADMAP.md`** under the now-item-less heading. Verified: item's header archived, its "This prose…" + "> blockquote" lines stayed behind — the record is split across two files, and the orphan prose then looks like dangling garbage. **`archive-closed.sh` (id:046a) does NOT have this bug** — its block boundary is "next top-level bullet OR heading", so it captures column-0 prose/blockquote correctly; the fix for roadmap-archive.sh is to adopt the same boundary rule (or consolidate the two archivers — see id:046a's "subsume/retire roadmap-archive.sh" open question). **(2) then-empty headers left behind — BOTH archivers.** After every item under a `##`/`###` grouping heading is archived, the emptied heading is deliberately left in place ("ROADMAP headers are structural — no section pruning"). The reporting session hit ROADMAP files littered with empty headers. This is a **design-judgment fork, not a clear bug:** some ROADMAP headings ARE persistent structure (e.g. a standing `## Current work`) and must NOT be pruned, but transient grouping headers (e.g. `## Review batch 2026-07-06`) should go with their items. Resolution options: (a) port `archive-done.sh`'s empty-non-protected-section pruning (name-protect a small set, prune the rest); (b) move the emptied heading INTO the archive alongside its block ("archived together with their items" — the reporter's phrasing) so the archive keeps the grouping context; (c) leave as-is and treat empty headers as acceptable. Decide (a)/(b)/(c) before coding — pairs with id:046a's consolidation decision and the [[todo-prune]] name-protection design. **Scope:** fix (1) mechanically (RED test: a `[x]` item with a column-0 prose line + a `>` blockquote → both move to archive, nothing stranded); (2) is gated on the a/b/c judgment. Relates to id:6b67 (built roadmap-archive.sh), id:046a (archive-closed consolidation), `tests/test_roadmap_archive.sh`. <!-- id:546b -->
- [x] [ROUTINE] **Relay pre-integrate isolation gate — a spawned child can write to the target's MAIN checkout instead of its own worktree** (observed 2026-07-14, loderite R2 consumer handoff). DISTINCT from the c6c8 `isolation:worktree`-param hazard: the child correctly RAN `git worktree add …` but then wrote every edit to `~/src/loderite` (repo-root-relative paths / never `cd`-ing into the worktree). Its worktree stayed empty (0 commits ahead of base), so its "commit in worktree" was a no-op and its self-report was wrong; the agent then wrongly concluded its new tests "weren't collected" (it had run `npm test` in the empty worktree). Cost: the whole handoff's RED specs landed loose in the main checkout, mixed with an unrelated in-flight edit, and had to be reconciled by hand. **RECOMMENDED FIX (3 parts):** (1) **PROMPT** — the child instruction must force the worktree as its working dir (absolute worktree path in every Read/Write/Edit, or make it cwd) and explicitly forbid touching the main checkout; fold this into the invariant-4 child-spawn boilerplate. (2) **INTEGRATOR GATE (mechanize — the load-bearing fix)** — a shared `scripts/verify-isolation.sh <worktree>` the integrator (invariant 5) runs BEFORE merging: assert `git -C <worktree> log --oneline origin/main..HEAD` is non-empty AND `git -C <worktree> status` is clean; if the worktree is empty while the target's main checkout is dirty with the child's work, isolation FAILED → fail loud, do not merge an empty branch. (3) **RECOVERY doctrine** — when it happens the work is usually sound but mislocated: finish/commit it in the MAIN checkout under the held lease (the id:15d5 pattern), salvage beats discard+re-run. Relates c6c8 (sibling isolation hazard), 15d5 (main-checkout-under-lease), d2cd (lock/hazard umbrella), the invariant-4 worktree spawn step + invariant-5 integrate step. **PROMOTED to ROADMAP 2026-07-15** (handoff run relay-20260715-121544-12169, single-id-two-views): [ROUTINE] with a functional RED spec `tests/test_verify_isolation.sh`; load-bearing deliverable = `relay/scripts/verify-isolation.sh` (fix part 2), parts 1+3 fold in as doc edits. <!-- id:f682 -->
- [x] **Make relay worktree/branch cleanup FORCE-FREE (respect a strict no-force policy)** (user 2026-07-15) — the relay pool's serialized integrator + cleanup runs **`git worktree remove --force`** (and relies on `git branch -D`), which BREAKS under a strict destructive-op guardrail (a user policy blocking `--force` / `rm -f` / `git reset --hard` / force-delete — see `docs/destructive-op-guardrail.md`): the force op is denied, the worktree isn't removed, and inert debris (orphaned worktrees + branches) accumulates **every run**. Worse, a `TaskStop`'d pool parks orphan worktrees that ALSO need `--force`/`rm -rf` to dispose. **FIX:** make cleanup force-free — before `git worktree remove` (NO `--force`), bring the worktree to a clean state (executors already commit per contract; for stray untracked/build files `git stash` or a scoped clean of KNOWN-throwaway paths), then remove without `--force`; on a genuine can't-remove, **surface it, never force**. Prefer `git worktree remove` (no flag) + fallback-to-stash over the defensive `--force`. Also audit ALL relay scripts (integrator recipe in SKILL.md §5, `relay-reconcile.sh`, `ckpt-tag.sh`, `git-lock-push.sh`) + `git-diary-workflow` for `--force`/`-f`/`reset --hard`/`rm -rf`/`branch -D`, and provide force-free paths or gate them behind explicit human confirmation (never auto — the `force-push.sh` confirm-gate pattern is the model). **Goal: a relay run under a strict no-force policy leaves NO debris and never ATTEMPTS a forbidden op.** Relates `docs/destructive-op-guardrail.md`, id:0902 (repo lease), the D1 orphan-park (id:689c), `relay-reconcile.sh`. **DONE 2026-07-15** (meeting `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-15-2227-relay-force-free-cleanup.md`, D1–D7): new force-free `relay/scripts/worktree-retire.sh` (plain `worktree remove` → `branch -d`/park; dirty ⇒ surface+leave, never force) called from reconcile reap/park + the relay-loop integrator prompt; `relay-reconcile.sh` integrate now `branch -d`, its human `--discard` gated behind `RELAY_DISCARD_CONFIRM=1` (force-push.sh model); executor contract v7→v8 clean-worktree exit gate (rule 5b) + review.md anti-gaming check; `git stash drop`/`clear` added to the guardrail; single-file `rm -f` de-cargo-culted repo-wide + `tools/check-no-bare-rm-f.sh` regression lint; `make test` 246/0. <!-- id:373e -->

- [x] **git-annex worktrees can NEVER be retired — `worktree-retire.sh` refuses forever and misreports it as "dirty"** — FIXED 2026-07-16 (same session). Root cause proven empirically: the `.git` symlink appears **immediately at `git worktree add`**, before any annex command — it is `filter.annex.process` (the smudge filter), NOT the annex `post-checkout` hook (hypothesis tested and DISPROVED: hooks-disabled still produced the symlink; zkWhale sets `core.hooksPath=tools/git-hooks`, so the annex hook was never active). Confirmed by construction: `worktree add` with the annex filters disabled yields a proper `gitdir:` file that removes cleanly. **Prevention at add-time REJECTED** — disabling the smudge filter checks annexed files out as raw pointer files; zkWhale annexes 4 snapshot JSONs and its relay items touch `snapshot:predeploy`, so a child could commit pointers as content. The symlink is deliberate annex design (annexed relative symlinks `../.git/annex/objects/...` must resolve inside the worktree), so fighting it at creation is wrong. **Fix shipped at the RETIREMENT side instead:** `worktree-retire.sh` now normalizes a symlinked `.git` back to git's own standard `gitdir:` pointer before removal — guarded (only when it resolves to THIS repo's own admin dir for THIS worktree; anything else surfaces untouched), non-destructive (rewrites only the pointer; admin dir/index/tree untouched), and force-free (plain `rm --`, no `-f`). The dirty check still runs after and still wins, so it cannot become a backdoor. Also fixed the reporting bug: `git worktree remove`'s stderr was swallowed (`2>&1` → `/dev/null`), which is what made a structural failure masquerade as "dirty" on a provably clean tree for ~5 weeks; the real git error is now surfaced verbatim. Also fixed the malformed double-`-C` in the deferral message. Covered by 2 new hermetic tests in `tests/test_worktree_retire.sh` (annex layout → retires; annex layout + dirty → still surfaced+left, work intact) incl. a vacuity guard asserting stock git really refuses. Reclaimed 1.2G (3 zkWhale worktrees retired, all clean+merged). Suite green 247/0. Relates id:373e (force-free retirement), id:6e02 (single-target scope), [[no-swallow-stderr]]. <!-- id:de4a -->

"Worktree empty" is the signature of BOTH a legit no-op AND a breach. Owner ratified the **main-HEAD discriminator**: `base = merge-base(worktree, main)` IS the dispatch-time main HEAD, so breach = `empty && main advanced by a NON-merge commit` — needs no pool plumbing. `--first-parent` keeps a sibling unit's merged branch commits from reading as a breach. - [x] **OWNER LOOK — yinyang-puzzle id:e01f landed by cherry-pick, not `--no-ff` merge** — **ACCEPTED by owner 2026-07-16, this instance only** (not a precedent for future cherry-pick integrations), on the stated condition that the outcome matched what the merge would have produced. **Condition VERIFIED before acceptance:** the pre-cherry-pick original survives as unreachable commit `b07cfcc`; its tree `e660e850…` is **byte-identical** to what landed (`0bb1da4`), and both share parent `90240be` — main had not diverged, so a `--no-ff` merge would have wrapped that exact tree. `git diff b07cfcc 0bb1da4` is empty. Only *topology* was lost (no merge commit recording branch ancestry), not content. Root cause of the cherry-pick itself was not pursued (accepted as a one-off). <!-- id:388f --> Reflog is decisive: `0bb1da4 main@{2026-07-15 17:06:31}: cherry-pick: feat(etch): consistent shared-edge arc-count etching (id:e01f)`. The child DID work in an isolated worktree (so `verify-isolation.sh` would have passed — this is **not** an isolation breach), but the integrator cherry-picked onto main instead of `--no-ff` merging, then deleted the branch (no ref survives). Related: commit `bc58a8f`'s subject claims "verify + **merge** arc_etch" but git shows no merge — the message is inaccurate though the work landed. **Cannot be adjudicated mechanically:** RELAY_LOG labels e01f's executor `(claude-sonnet, relay-loop)` while its handoff entry says `reviewer handoff (claude-opus-4-8, Q4-mockup session)` — a supervised session, and per id:15d5 supervised direct-to-main writes are legitimate by design. So this is either a merge-protocol deviation or a sanctioned supervised integration; **the distinction is the owner's call**, not a delegated verdict. If it was the pool, the `--no-ff` invariant (guardrail 1) was bypassed and that wants a root-cause. <!-- id:388f --> `zkWhale` is the **only** `git-annex` repo across all own repos (`annex.uuid` set; no other repo has `.git/annex`), and it was the **only** repo with lingering relay worktrees (3 dirs, **1.2G**, from runs 07-04/07-10/07-11 — all clean, all fully merged, holding no unmerged work). **Mechanism:** git-annex replaces a linked worktree's `.git` **file** with a **symlink** to the admin dir, so `git worktree remove` fails validation permanently: `fatal: validation failed, cannot remove working tree: '<wt>/.git' is not a .git file, error code 10`. This is structural — `--force` would not help (validation precedes it), so no force-free *or* forced retirement can ever succeed. Every relay run on an annex repo therefore leaks a worktree forever. **Second defect (reporting):** `worktree-retire.sh` maps this to `exit 3 "worktree dirty/unremovable — LEFT on disk"` and advises "commit real work / gitignore throwaway" — actively misleading, since `git status --porcelain` is EMPTY. It conflates a dirty tree (a correct surface-and-leave) with a structural failure (a permanent leak that no amount of committing fixes). **Fix candidates:** (a) detect the symlink-`.git` case explicitly and emit a distinct exit code + accurate message naming git-annex; (b) decide the sanctioned repair — restoring the standard `gitdir:` file makes the canonical removal work, but that is git-internals surgery and was DENIED by the destructive-op guardrail when attempted here (correctly — it forces past a safety gate), so it needs an explicit owner decision + a guardrail-legible path; (c) consider whether relay should worktree annex repos at all. **NOTE:** the 3 zkWhale worktrees are still on disk (1.2G unreclaimed) pending (b). Cosmetic: the deferral message prints a malformed `git -C <repo> -C <worktree> status` (double `-C`). Relates id:373e (force-free retirement), id:6e02 (single-target scope). <!-- id:de4a -->
- [x] **`test_isolation_gate_wired.sh` was FLAKY: a >64 KB `printf | grep -q` under `set -o pipefail` spuriously red-lit the whole suite** (found + fixed 2026-07-16 by the relay review child, run relay-20260716-125514-23493) — the test piped `$loop_code` (relay-loop.js, 91697 B) into `grep -q`. The pipe buffer is 65536 B, so `printf` BLOCKS mid-write while `grep -q` matches at byte 63529 and exits FIRST; `printf` then dies of SIGPIPE (141) and `pipefail` promotes that to a pipeline failure — **even though grep matched** (proven: `rc=141 PIPESTATUS=[0]`). Pure race: measured **1/25 idle, 22/40 under CPU load**. Blast radius was the definition-of-done gate itself — a spurious red that indicts the id:7612 isolation gate rather than the test, exactly the signal the suite exists to make trustworthy. **Fixed**: herestrings (no early-exiting reader ⇒ no SIGPIPE) + `grep -m1` for `| head -1`; 0/60 after, and all 3 mutations (gate call removed / repo-relative path / ABORT stripped) still correctly caught, so the spec was not weakened. Note the diagnosis needs a real `bash` — the agent Bash tool is `zsh`, where `PIPESTATUS` is empty and the race does not reproduce. <!-- id:b780 -->

(2) *"`make status` reports per-skill, not per-file, so it could not have caught a 2-of-64 gap"* — **FALSE**: `make status` honors `DEST_DIR` AND reports per file; against a simulated drop it prints the exact line `!! scripts/lib-anchored-id.sh (not installed)`. **ACTUAL ROOT CAUSE:** the detector already exists and is already precise — **nothing invokes it**. The repo is consumed through per-file symlinks in `~/.claude`, so any new file is invisible to every consumer until a human remembers `make install`, and the failure surfaces loudly only later, in an unrelated repo's session. This is the SAME class as [[id:de36]] (`todo-conformance.sh` correctly flagged the acc7 line; nothing ran it) and the same rule: CLAUDE.md mechanize-first — *a loud detector whose invocation is optional is not a detector*. **Scope: wire the existing check into a routine flow — do NOT build a new detector.** Recommended home: `relay/scripts/relay-doctor.sh` (`/relay health`, id:9bec), which already exists to answer "is this environment sound?" — an install-drift check is exactly its remit. **A drift test in `tests/` is NOT the answer**: CLAUDE.md §Testing requires tests be hermetic and never touch `~/.claude`, so a suite test cannot read the real install tree; the hermetic half (does `make install-<skill>` install everything declared?) already passes today and would NOT have caught this. The check must inspect the LIVE environment, which is `relay-doctor`'s job, not the suite's. **Mandatory wrinkle — the guard must not cry wolf:** `make status` currently reports one legitimate `!!` — `meeting-cross: SKILL.md (not installed)` — because that alias skill is **deliberately** uninstalled pending deletion ([[id:4f5f]]). Any drift check MUST treat deprecated/intentionally-absent skills as expected, or it fires on day one and everyone learns to ignore it. - [x] **BUG — relay-loop returns `handbacks: []` while its OWN event log records a handback: a parked orphan is silently dropped from the run summary** — user 2026-07-17 ("file the bug"), found only because a human happened to run `/relay reconcile .`. REPRODUCED END-TO-END on run `relay-20260717-100452-13146` (loderite, `/relay --intensive .`): the execute child fixed `id:4c02` (portrait menu overflow), committed `ea0a7c5`, and the integrator hit a **ROADMAP.md merge conflict**, correctly `git merge --abort`ed, and parked the branch as `relay/orphan/relay-20260717-100452-13146-execute`. The event log captured it perfectly — `{"kind":"handback","repo":"loderite","mode":"execute","reason":"Merge conflict in ROADMAP.md when running `git merge --no-ff …` (RELAY_LOG.md auto-merged fine). Ran `git merge --abort`; main is clean… left on disk for supervised reconcile"}` — **but the Workflow's returned summary said `completed:[{mode:"review"}], handbacks:[], queuedRemaining:[]`**, i.e. the run reported total success while a green, wanted fix sat unmerged on a parked ref. The front door prints "the HANDBACK count" from that summary (SKILL.md step 4), so the operator is told **zero**. This is precisely the CLAUDE.md *"a deterministic detector that FINDS a problem but whose resolution silently no-ops"* anti-pattern, in its most expensive form: detection was loud AND durable, the summary silently swallowed it. VERIFIED the parked work is genuine, not gamed: `tests/menu-scroll.test.ts` (the `4c02` RED spec) is **4-failed on main, 4-passed on the branch**; the diff implements the two `throw new Error("not implemented (roadmap:4c02)")` stubs in `src/hud/menu-layout.ts` and wires them into `src/menu.ts`. FIX: the returned summary MUST be derived from (or reconciled against) the same event stream that recorded the handback — a `kind:"handback"` event with no corresponding entry in `handbacks[]` should be impossible; consider asserting that invariant in `relay-loop.js` before return, and failing loudly if it trips. ROOT CAUSE of the conflict itself (separate but co-dispatched): the pool ran an **execute AND a review for the SAME repo in the same run** — the execute child ticked `4c02`'s box while the review child rewrote `ROADMAP.md` to promote `7ccf`+`a78b`, and ROADMAP.md is explicitly NOT `merge=union` (checkbox toggles can't union — SKILL.md Guardrails). So an execute+review pair on one repo is a near-guaranteed ledger collision; the D3 class order (execute→review) sequences the *dispatch* but nothing stops both landing in one run against a shared ledger. - [x] [ROUTINE] **append.sh inbox write-path integrity — validate, mint-inside, echo-what-was-written** — decided 2026-07-17 (meeting `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-17-1450-acc7-phantom-append-write-integrity.md`, D2/D3). `routed:acc7` was minted, reported as filed, and never written: the loderite hand-run escaped `$ID` in the payload but not in its own `echo "filed routed:$ID"`, so bash wrote a literal `$ID` while the receipt said `acc7` — and `loderite/TODO.md:40` (id:0c54) then cited a token that existed nowhere. Root cause is not the escaping: `-t inbox` validates nothing and prints nothing on success (`meeting/append.sh:283-287`), so the caller invents its own receipt (id:1735 class — and the item being filed was *about* that class). Three changes, `-t inbox` only: **(A)** reject a non-conforming entry (non-zero, nothing appended); **(B)** `--route-to <repo> -e "<desc>"` mints + builds + writes the line itself; **(C)** always echo the token *actually written* (minted, or parsed back from the appended line). Fold-in: the mint collision-checks the **routed** namespace via a new `scan-routed-tokens <target>` verb mirroring `scan-ids` — `scan_ids` greps `id:[0-9a-f]{4}` over `<root>` only, so `routed:` tokens are minted unchecked today. Out of scope: restricting the raw `-e` form; validating `discoveries`/`personas`. RED spec `tests/test_inbox_write_integrity.sh` (verified red 2026-07-17 — it reproduces the acc7 incident against current code). Execution twin in ROADMAP.md (single-id-two-views D2). <!-- id:34c2 -->

- [x] **[INPUT — meeting] `CHANGELOG.md` across the fleet — user-facing changes (+ relevant backend), bucketed by sensible time ranges (e.g. daily)** (user 2026-07-16) — "especially for the semver repos but in general". Today **25 own repos carry `v*` tags** (loderite 49 tags, zkm 23, zkm-ner 22, zkm-eml 16, zkWhale 13, … down to 1-tag repos) and **none has a CHANGELOG**: the only per-version record is the tag message + `git log`, which is unreadable as a "what changed for me" summary. Scope per the user: the most important **user-facing** changes, but **also relevant backend/internal** ones (not a strict keep-a-changelog "user-visible only" filter) — and **summarized by sensible buckets / time ranges (e.g. daily)** rather than one line per commit. **Why now:** the 2026-07-16 session bumped loderite 0.40→0.45, chidiai 0.1→0.13, zkm 0.18→0.21 — i.e. **20 releases' worth of closes** landed with no human-readable record of what each contained; the version numbers alone carry no information. **Design questions for the meeting:** (1) **derive vs hand-write** — the relay already knows every close (`workedIds` per integrate, the `relay-ckpt-*` tag messages, RELAY_LOG.md), so a CHANGELOG is arguably *derivable* rather than authored (prefer derive-or-guard per id:415b; a hand-maintained changelog drifts exactly like the diagrams in id:a17a). (2) **bucketing** — daily vs per-release vs both (a release spans days; a day spans repos). (3) **the user-facing/backend split** — one list with tags, or two sections? (4) **who writes it** — this is a **sibling of [[id:e647]]**, which already rules that the version bump is *the reviewer's job at integrate, NOT the executor in a worktree* (parallel worktrees collide on the manifest/lockfile); a changelog entry has the **identical** collision profile, so it should almost certainly ride the same integrate-time hook rather than being an executor duty. Decide e647 and this together. (5) **per-repo vs central** — 25 repos × a CHANGELOG each, or the `claude-diary` as the cross-repo narrative with per-repo files only where a consumer exists? (6) **retroactivity** — generate history from existing tags/RELAY_LOG, or start from now? **NOTE — this REOPENS a ratified decision for THIS repo only:** `CLAUDE.md` §Versioning records "A public-repo `CHANGELOG.md` is **deferred** — trigger is the first external consumer who needs to pin a version for a reproducible install (none exists today; `git log` covers the rest)" (D-A/id:8ef3, meeting 2026-07-12-1030). dotclaude-skills also has **no repo version by design** (git = SSOT), so it is the *weakest* candidate in the fleet. The user's ask is fleet-wide and names the semver repos specifically; it does not obviously overturn 8ef3's reasoning for the manifest-less repo. **Do not silently override 8ef3** — the meeting must either honour it (dotclaude-skills exempt, semver repos adopt) or explicitly amend it with the owner's say.  **DECIDED 2026-07-17 (meeting `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-17-1541-semver-trigger-and-fleet-changelog.md`, D2/D3/D4 — owner-ratified):** the CHANGELOG is **DERIVED at integrate** from existing relay state (`workedIds`, `relay-ckpt-*` tag messages, `RELAY_LOG.md`), **starting from now — never backfilled** (per-close tags are unrecoverable after the 2026-07-16 batch, so generated history would be plausible and unverifiable). **If it needs a new per-item 'user-facing?' field, this decision is WRONG and must come back** — that is authoring with extra steps. Home: **per-repo CHANGELOG.md in every semver repo**, release-bucketed (D4). **id:8ef3 EXPLICITLY AMENDED (D3)**: dotclaude-skills DOES get a CHANGELOG but still **no version** — date-bucketed per relay integrate, since with no manifest there is no bump to key off. Amendment basis on record: 8ef3 weighed only EXTERNAL consumers and correctly found none; this repo is consumed INTERNALLY via per-file symlinks by every other repo's sessions — a class it never considered. An explicit amendment on an unconsidered premise, NOT a reinterpretation. CLAUDE.md §Versioning updated to match. Ships together with id:e647. READY TO BUILD. **DERIVER LANDED 2026-07-18 (this repo only, stays OPEN):** `relay/scripts/changelog-append.sh` (deterministic, flock'd, atomic; date-bucket for version-less repos + `--version` release-bucket for semver; **opt-in — no-op unless CHANGELOG.md already exists**, which is the D4-safety that keeps it OFF semver repos until e647 bootstraps them) + integrator wiring in `relay-loop.js` step 2b (derive-at-integrate from `report.summary`+worked-ids, scoped-add commit) + this repo's `CHANGELOG.md` bootstrapped date-bucketed per D3 + `tests/test_changelog_derive.sh` (8 cases, green; full suite 258/0). **REMAINS (D4 ships-together):** id:e647 bump-trigger + per-repo `CHANGELOG.md` bootstrap across the semver fleet (release-bucketed). **OWNER SEQUENCING DECISION PENDING:** the deriver is proven for version-less repos; whether to build e647 next (D4 together) or let the deriver bake here first (the recorded Riku/Orla dissent) is the owner's call. **UPDATE 2026-07-18 — MECHANISM COMPLETE (e647 landed, `6c5f84f`, suite 260/0):** the deriver AND the release-bucket wiring are both on main — `version-bump.sh` (step 2a) now supplies `--version` to `changelog-append.sh` (step 2b), so a semver repo release-buckets and a version-less repo date-buckets, automatically at integrate. - [x] [ROUTINE] **`append.sh -t inbox` swallows its validator's diagnostic when the relay skill is absent** — REVIEW FINDING 2026-07-17 from the id:34c2 integration (verified, not speculative). id:34c2's executor validates by shelling out to `relay/scripts/todo-conformance.sh --inbox` (good reuse — one definition of "conforming line", no NIH), which introduces a NEW runtime coupling from the **meeting** skill to the **relay** skill. Probed the dependency-absent case (`make install-meeting` without relay, i.e. no sibling `relay/scripts/`): behaviour is **FAIL-CLOSED and therefore SAFE** — exit 127, nothing appended, no acc7 reintroduction, because `set -e` catches the failed command substitution. **But the diagnostic is SWALLOWED**: `conf_out="$("$conf_sh" --inbox "$tmp_check" 2>&1)"` captures "No such file or directory" into `conf_out`, which is discarded when `set -e` fires — so the caller gets a bare exit 127 with **zero explanation**. That is a silent-swallow, which this repo bans (CLAUDE.md no-silent-swallow / mechanize-first "fail LOUDLY"; [[no-swallow-stderr]]). **Root cause is the RED spec (`tests/test_inbox_write_integrity.sh`, authored by the 2026-07-17 handoff) never covering the dependency-absent case** — the executor met the contract as written; this is a spec gap, not executor misbehaviour. Fix: probe `[[ -x "$conf_sh" ]]` first and fail LOUDLY with a message naming the missing dependency; and decide whether the meeting→relay coupling is acceptable at all, or whether the conforming-form grammar should live somewhere both skills can reach. Extend the RED spec to pin the loud failure. See `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-17-1450-acc7-phantom-append-write-integrity.md`. — DONE 2026-07-18, covered by tests (tests/test_inbox_write_integrity.sh bbb2 case): `append.sh` now probes `[[ -x "$conf_sh" ]]` BEFORE the command substitution and fails LOUDLY (exit 3) naming the missing `todo-conformance.sh`/relay dependency, appending nothing — the silent exit-127 swallow is gone. (The meeting→relay coupling itself is accepted as-is; no relocation of the conforming-form grammar.) <!-- id:bbb2 -->

- [x] [INBOUND routed:38db from truncocraft 2026-06-29] Make 'bump version on closed-work trigger' a global default (or discuss): global CLAUDE.md Versioning defines how to bump but never when, so repos sit at 0.1.0 indefinitely (truncocraft: 296 commits, 0 vX.Y.Z tags); decide global trigger (per closed ROADMAP item) vs per-repo opt-in. RELAY DIMENSION: bump must be the reviewer's job at integrate (post --no-ff merge, on main, same checkpoint turn) NOT the executor in a worktree (parallel worktrees collide on package.json/lockfile); bump commit must leave tree clean or clean-tree-gate.sh defers the repo; readers must use `git describe --match 'v[0-9]*'` since relay-ckpt-* tags outnumber v*. Keep prose-only for a few cycles (observe-before-preventing) before any relay-loop mechanization. **OBSERVATION EVIDENCE 2026-07-16 (the cycles this item was waiting for — the drift is now measured, not hypothesized).** A single relay session shipped 23 units across 12 repos; three repos were checked for version drift and **all three had shipped every close unversioned**: **loderite** 5 user-observable closes past v0.40.0 (its own CLAUDE.md mandates a bump per user-observable close), **zkm** 3 past v0.18.0, **chidiai** 12 past v0.1.0. Owner ruled "bump now, one per close" → loderite **v0.45.0**, chidiai **v0.13.0**, zkm **v0.21.0** (retroactive batch commits; per-close tags are unrecoverable after the fact). Fleet context: **25 own repos carry `v*` tags**, so this is not a three-repo problem. **Three findings that sharpen this item's design:** (a) **the diagnosis "the executor contract is silent" is a red herring** — the silence is CORRECT per this item's own ruling (the executor must NOT bump); the gap is that the *reviewer* side was never built, so nobody bumps. Anyone re-reading this should not "fix" the executor contract. (b) **`git describe --match 'v[0-9]*'` — this item's prescribed reader — SILENTLY MISREPORTS on zkm**: its `[autotag]` hook creates **lightweight** tags (`git cat-file -t v0.21.0` → `commit`, not `tag`; same for v0.18.0/v0.17.0; only the ancient v0.2.0 is annotated), and `git describe` ignores lightweight tags without `--tags` → it reported **`v0.2.0-622-g448580f`** on a HEAD tagged v0.21.0, i.e. 622 commits and 19 minor versions stale. **The reader must be `git describe --tags --match 'v[0-9]*'`**, or the hook must annotate. Worth its own fix — a version reader that is confidently 19 versions wrong is worse than none. (c) **the cascade is already tooled and the bump must go through it**: zkm's pre-push hook BLOCKS a bump whose 18 plugin `uv.lock`s are stale and names `scripts/relock-plugins.sh --push`; any mechanization here must call that tool, not re-implement the cascade (a hand-rolled loop relocked correctly but skipped the commits, leaving 17 repos dirty — chidiai case `improvised-a-tool-past-the-repo-s-own`). **Sibling: [[id:b8fa]]** (fleet CHANGELOG) has the IDENTICAL collision profile (an integrate-time write to a shared file that parallel worktrees would clobber) — decide the two together; one integrate-time hook plausibly serves both.  **DECIDED 2026-07-17 (meeting `docs/meeting-notes/2026-07-17-1541-semver-trigger-and-fleet-changelog.md`, D1/D4 — owner-ratified):** the standing trigger is a **global default**: the **reviewer bumps at integrate, once per user-observable close**, tagging it and regenerating the lockfile in the SAME commit. The judgement stays with the reviewer (a refactor close must NOT bump — 'user-observable' is not derivable, which is why full derivation was rejected). Confirms this item's own relay dimension: never the executor in a worktree (manifest+lockfile collide across parallel worktrees). Per D4 this ships **together with id:b8fa**, overriding the recommended pilot-first sequencing — recorded dissent: it lands in the expensive reviewer turn already doing roadmap re-derivation + test audit + merge, a botched bump stalls the repo via clean-tree-gate.sh, and zkm's parent bump cascades to every plugin uv.lock. READY TO BUILD. **DONE 2026-07-18** (background-built, apex-reviewed, merged `6c5f84f`; suite 260/0): `relay/scripts/version-bump.sh` — reviewer bumps at integrate per user-observable close (`--level` is the reviewer's non-derivable judgement, D1), manifest detect (pyproject/package.json) with version-less repos a no-op, loose-0.x, injectable lockfile regen (`$VERSION_BUMP_LOCK_CMD`), scoped clean-tree commit (id:debf), **annotated** `vX.Y.Z` tag (finding b), zkm cascade via the repo's own `scripts/relock-plugins.sh` (finding c, never reimplemented).
