- [x] [ROUTINE] **Something silently re-nests top-level `title:`/`hook:` under `metadata:` on memory-file writes, defeating `memory-index.py`'s field resolution** — OBSERVED TWICE this session (2026-07-17), verified not speculative. Two memory files were authored with `title:` and `hook:` as TOP-LEVEL frontmatter keys (the shape id:2e6d's `tools/memory-index.py` reads: most-specific-first `title:`→`name:`→stem, `hook:`→`description:`). On the next read both keys had been relocated **under the `metadata:` block** (`metadata.title`, `metadata.hook`), so `memory-index.py` found neither at top level and **silently fell back** to `description:` (for the hook) and the filename (for the title) — producing a verbose, wrong index line with no error. Fixed each time by re-hoisting the keys and regenerating, but the corruption is silent and recurring. **UNKNOWN AND MUST BE ESTABLISHED BEFORE FIXING (do not guess the culprit — this session already mis-diagnosed id:1102 twice by asserting a cause before checking):** WHICH writer re-nests them — candidates are the `Write`/`Edit` tool path, a frontmatter normalizer/linter, the `claude-sessions-backup` commit, or `memory-index.py --write` itself round-tripping. Reproduce by writing a file with top-level `title:`/`hook:`, then observing which operation moves them. **Then decide the fix per the mechanize-first rule:** either make the responsible writer preserve key position, OR make `memory-index.py` resolve `title:`/`hook:` from BOTH top-level AND `metadata.*` (tolerate the nesting rather than fight it) — the latter dissolves it if the re-nester can't be controlled, but must be a conscious choice, not a shrug. This is a [[memory-index-derived-2e6d]] frontmatter-format hazard: the index is only correct if its inputs survive a write. Relates the [[no-swallow-stderr]] doctrine — the fallback to `description:` should arguably be LOUD (warn when a file has `metadata.hook` but no top-level `hook:`, which is almost certainly this bug). <!-- id:e875 -->
- [x] [ROUTINE] **`tests/test_resource_claim_pid.sh` is FLAKY in the full suite (breaks the "make test green = done" gate)** — observed 2026-06-25 while shipping id:2dea: the test passes 3/3 in isolation but fails ~50% of full-suite runs (byte-identical reruns gave fail / pass-104 / fail) with "a stale-mtime claim with a LIVE live_pid was stolen — PID-liveness not honored" — i.e. `claim.sh::is_live` intermittently false-negatives on test 1's live `--pid` claim. Suspect root cause: `pid_alive()` (claim.sh:99-105) reads `jq -r '.live_pid' "$f" 2>/dev/null` and treats ANY transient read failure as empty→dead (the `2>/dev/null` swallow, cf. [[feedback-mechanize-no-swallow-stderr]]); under full-suite load a slow/interrupted jq or a background-`sleep`/PID-reuse race in the test harness (the `( trap - EXIT; exec sleep 600 ) & LIVE_PID=$!` anchor at L36) makes `kill -0` miss. **Fix directions:** (a) harden the harness — verify `kill -0 $LIVE_PID` succeeds right before the assertion and retry/poll instead of one-shot, and confirm no other test's cleanup signals it; (b) make `pid_alive` distinguish "jq failed to read" from "live_pid absent" (don't swallow a read error into a false "dead"); (c) if it's genuine non-determinism, mark the timing-sensitive assertion accordingly. A flaky claim-liveness test is corrosive because every future item's done-check runs `make test`. Pre-existing in id:1b11 (NOT introduced by id:2dea — that test is green every run). <!-- id:ab5c -->
- [x] [ROUTINE] **Relay executor children must run with a FAILING askpass so a sub-process `sudo` can never pop a GUI password prompt** — OBSERVED 2026-07-18 (run relay-20260717-182134-8632): a loderite `execute` child running headless-browser e2e/screenshot work (`npx playwright test` for id:e43a) triggered a graphical sudo password dialog at 01:03:36 (`sudo[2330298]: auth could not identify password`) — almost certainly Playwright's `install-deps` reaching for `sudo apt-get`. The user was prompted and dismissed it (no privilege granted, child continued green). **The executor contract already says "missing dep → handback, not sudo" ([[no-sudo-pamac]]) — but that is PROSE, and prose can't stop a *sub-process* (playwright) from calling sudo.** Mechanical fix: dispatch every relay child (and ideally the whole pool env) with `SUDO_ASKPASS=/bin/false` (or run children where `sudo` resolves to `sudo -n`), so any sudo attempt fails INSTANTLY and non-interactively — no dialog ever reaches the user; the child just gets a non-zero exit and hands back the missing dep. Verify the child still surfaces the dep in its handback rather than silently swallowing the failure ([[feedback-mechanize-no-swallow-stderr]]). Relates the id:077d mechanize-role-boundaries idea, but note a pre-commit hook does NOT catch this (sudo is a runtime command, not a git write). Done-check: a child whose task shells out to `sudo` gets an immediate non-interactive failure (no GUI prompt) and hands back. **PARTIAL FIX 2026-07-19 (relay human):** `SUDO_ASKPASS=/bin/false` added to `~/.claude/settings.json` `env` — an AFK-safe naive-case catch (a subprocess sudo inheriting the env fails non-interactively → child hands back, no GUI dialog). A `deny Bash(sudo *)` rule was REJECTED: the permission matcher sees the wrapper command (`npx playwright test`), NOT the inner subprocess sudo, so it would miss this exact case — and it blocks AFK. This is defense-in-depth, NOT containment (any process can re-export `SUDO_ASKPASS`); real containment = the separate-OS-user route **id:5937**. Marked done as a partial fix; id:5937 is the real one. <!-- id:eb46 -->
- [x] [ROUTINE] **model-probe.sh: grade arm uses `echo "$output"` (flag/escape swallowing)** — audit id:401c Run 11 (Pass 1 finding). `echo "$output" | grep -qP "$regex"` mis-handles output starting with `-n`/`-e`/`-E` or containing backslashes; `printf '%s\n' "$output"` is robust. Zero impact today (battery goldens are numbers/words) but behaviour-adjacent forward-robustness. LOW severity, -sized (one-line change + a battery case with a leading-dash/backslash golden). <!-- id:b9b5 -->

Fail LOUD, non-zero. Wire as a PostToolUse hook on Write/Edit to `MEMORY.md` so it *enforces* rather than advises. **IRREDUCIBLE residual → independent review, narrowly scoped:** a hook can preserve every token yet drift in meaning ("defer refuter fleet" → "refuter fleet" inverts it). Mechanical cannot decide that; an LLM reviewer should fire ONLY on entries whose hook text changed, and must fail loudly ([[feedback-mechanize-reliability-not-cost]] — no LLM where mechanical is ≥ as good). **STRUCTURAL DISSOLUTION (decide first — this may delete the guard):** every one of the 108 files already carries `description:` frontmatter, so `MEMORY.md` could be **GENERATED** by enumerating the directory, making a dropped pointer *unrepresentable* rather than merely detected — exactly [[ledger-derived-index-decision-2840]]'s md=SSOT/index=cache shape, and "prefer dissolving a problem structurally over guarding it". **Open fork:** hooks are hand-tuned and terser than `description:` today, so generation needs either (a) `description:` becomes the hook (one source, lose the terse/verbose split) or (b) a new `hook:` frontmatter field. Pick the fork before building the lint, else the lint guards a file that's about to become derived. **PARTIAL FIX LANDED 2026-07-10** (~/.claude/projects commit 83d81fa0): the 3 orphans are resolved — `relay-fable-down-two-switch` + `feedback-fable-optional-not-gate` now carry index lines (the former SUPERSEDES `fable-down-flag`: it records the user calling `-d` mis-designed after an outage cost 18 handbacks — it was invisible to recall for ~4 weeks), and `feedback-canonical-paths` was an exact duplicate of `feedback-edit-canonical-paths` and was deleted. Also add an archive-eligibility rule (never archive a `feedback-*` entry — durable user preferences) and a supersession check (an entry whose hook says SUPERSEDES X should sort above X, or X should be archived). The one-shot invariant checker used for this pass (entries / link targets / per-entry `id:`+`routed:`+`[[link]]`+status-lexeme diff vs baseline) is the lint's spec — mechanize it. **FORK DECIDED + DISSOLUTION SHIPPED 2026-07-10** (dotclaude-skills a4cb9b4; ~/.claude/projects 409ea3cc): chose a new optional `hook:` frontmatter field over reusing `description:` — descriptions are as long or longer than the curated hooks, so `description:`-as-hook would GROW the file the ceiling is trying to shrink, and the two fields have different jobs (relevance summary vs index one-liner).
